### Post by el mariachi on 2008-05-31
**June 2008 Desktops - Posting Guidelines**
[SIZE=1]Read the rules before posting/submitting a screenshot of you Desktop![/SIZE]


:arrow: Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.

:arrow: If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.

:arrow: Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.

:arrow: The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.

:arrow: The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.

:arrow: Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.

:arrow: To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request that you format your posts in the following order:


Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).


**[COLOR=red]Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.[/COLOR]**

### Post by Ub1476 on 2008-06-01
> **weems said:**
> I really like your wallpaper. Link?

[http://interfacelift.com/wallpaper/details.php?id=1537](http://interfacelift.com/wallpaper/details.php?id=1537)

> **freduardo said:**
> Looks very good!

Any particular font configuration you could share? (like e.g. ~/.fonts.conf)


Fonts from rc.xml (obconf):
```
    <font place="ActiveWindow">
      <name>Liberation Sans</name>
      <size>8</size>
      <!-- font size in points -->
      <weight>Bold</weight>
      <!-- 'bold' or 'normal' -->
      <slant>Normal</slant>
      <!-- 'italic' or 'normal' -->
    </font>
    <font place="InactiveWindow">
      <name>Liberation Sans</name>
      <size>8</size>
      <!-- font size in points -->
      <weight>Bold</weight>
      <!-- 'bold' or 'normal' -->
      <slant>Normal</slant>
      <!-- 'italic' or 'normal' -->
    </font>
    <font place="MenuHeader">
      <name>Liberation Sans</name>
      <size>8</size>
      <!-- font size in points -->
      <weight>Bold</weight>
      <!-- 'bold' or 'normal' -->
      <slant>Normal</slant>
      <!-- 'italic' or 'normal' -->
    </font>
    <font place="MenuItem">
      <name>Liberation Sans</name>
      <size>8</size>
      <!-- font size in points -->
      <weight>Normal</weight>
      <!-- 'bold' or 'normal' -->
      <slant>Normal</slant>
      <!-- 'italic' or 'normal' -->
    </font>
    <font place="OnScreenDisplay">
      <name>Liberation Sans</name>
      <size>8</size>
      <!-- font size in points -->
      <weight>Normal</weight>
      <!-- 'bold' or 'normal' -->
      <slant>Normal</slant>
      <!-- 'italic' or 'normal' -->
    </font>
```

Basically just Liberation Sans 8, normal.

.Xdefaults file (urxvt terminal):
```
Xft*dpi:                96
Xft*antialias:          true
Xft*hinting:            full

Xcursor.theme: ComixCursors-Blue-Small

URxvt.termName: rxvt
URxvt.transparent: true
URxvt.inheritPixmap: False
URxvt.scrollBar: false
URxvt.saveLines: 5000
URxvt.urlLauncher:      firefox3
URxvt.cursorBlink: true
URxvt.geometry: 85x21
URxvt.fading: 15%
URxvt.shading: 75
urxvt.font:             xft:DejaVu Sans Mono:pixelsize=9
urxvt.boldFont:         xft:DejaVu Sans Mono:bold:pixelsize=10
!URxvt*background:      [80]#ece9e2
!URxvt.foreground: [80]#3d352a
urxvt.depth: 32
urxvt.background: rgba:0000/0000/0000/aaaa
urxvt.foreground: rgba:ffff/ffff/ffff/aaaa
URxvt.tintColor: #d9d7d1
URxvt.borderLess: true
!URxvt.InternalBorder: .5
URxvt.externalBorder: .5
URxvt.borderColor: #acacac

*foreground:     rgba:0000/0000/0000/dddd
*background:     rgb:10/10/10
!black
*color0:         rgb:20/20/20
*color8:         rgb:75/77/73
!red
*color1:         rgb:cc/00/00  
*color9:         rgb:ef/29/29
!green
*color2:         rgb:4e/9a/06
*color10:        rgb:8a/e2/34
!brown/yellow
*color3:         rgb:c4/a0/00
*color11:        rgb:fc/e9/4f
!blue
*color4:         rgb:34/65/a4
*color12:        rgb:72/9f/cf
!magenta
*color5:         rgb:75/50/7b
*color13:        rgb:ad/7f/a8
!cyan
*color6:         rgb:06/98/9a
*color14:        rgb:34/e2/e2
!white
*color7:         rgb:d3/d7/cf
*color15:        rgb:ee/ee/ec


```

Created by Reason, at least it's him I got it from.

That's all I can think of.

### Post by klange on 2008-06-01
> **Ub1476 said:**
> Hm, is Freewins useful anything? Is it some kind of base for an exciting future project, or is it just cool?

Just asking:)

With the lack of input redirection, it's still only good for looks, but it's a lot more stable and smooth now and also does scaling. Once SmSpillaz picked up the project, it really got a lot better. Still has its share of bugs, though, and again, without input redirection it's really just a gimmick. I can say from experience it's nice to have while watching videos and such when combined with the Ghost plugin (which disables input on "ghosted" windows).

[0.7.6 release information](http://guillaume.segu.in/blog/home/124/compiz-fusion-076-released/)

---

### Post by ayoli on 2008-06-02
> **diafanos said:**
> very nice conky!
Can you show us the config file?

sure, here you go :
```

background yes
#background no
use_xft yes
#xftfont Myriad pro:normal:size=9
xftfont Glisp:normal:size=9

xftalpha 1.0
update_interval 3.0
total_run_times 0
double_buffer yes

own_window yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type normal 		#or : desktop
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

#own_window no
#own_window_type normal
#own_window_transparent yes
#own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

minimum_size 220 5
maximum_width 690 5

draw_shades no ### SHADOW ###
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders yes

default_outline_color black
default_color white ### Text Color ###
default_shade_color black

alignment top_right
gap_x 16
gap_y 32

no_buffers yes
cpu_avg_samples 2

override_utf8_locale yes
#uppercase yes

TEXT
   ${font StyleBats:size=16}a${font}${voffset -1} ${cpu cpu0}%   ${font StyleBats:size=16}${voffset -7}a${font}${voffset -1} ${cpu cpu1}%    ${font StyleBats:size=16}${voffset -7}g${font}${voffset -1} ${memperc}%    ${font StyleBats:size=16}${voffset -7}i${font}${voffset -1} ${swapperc}%    ${font StyleBats:size=16}${voffset -7}4${font}${voffset -1} ${if_mounted /home}${fs_free  /home}${else}--${endif}    ${font StyleBats:size=16}${voffset -7}x${font}${voffset -1} ${if_mounted /media/store}${fs_free  /media/store}${else}--${endif}    ${font PizzaDude Bullets:size=14}${voffset -7}M${font}${voffset 1} ${if_existing /sys/class/net/eth0/operstate up}${upspeed eth0} Kb/s${else}${if_existing /sys/class/net/wlan0/operstate up}${upspeed wlan0} Kb/s${else}--${endif}${endif}    ${font PizzaDude Bullets:size=14}${voffset -6}S${font}${voffset 1} ${if_existing /sys/class/net/eth0/operstate up}${downspeed eth0} Kb/s${else}${if_existing /sys/class/net/wlan0/operstate up}${downspeed wlan0} Kb/s${else}--${endif}${endif}    ${exec /home/ayoli/local/bin/bat_state}${if_existing /home/ayoli/.bat_state charged}${font StyleBats:size=16}${voffset -6}o${else}${font StyleBats:size=16}${voffset -6}p${endif}${font}${voffset -2} ${battery_percent C1AB}%    

```
Note that you'll need StyleBats and PizzaDude Bullets fonts available on dafont.com.
You also may need to adjust the network interfaces and mount points.
Have fun :)

---

Very nice!  I like bright, or light-colored desktops.  The dark themes are cool to look at in threads like these, but I can't actually work in a dark theme for very long.  Hard on the eyes, and brings my spirit down.

### Post by cookieofdoom on 2008-06-03
> **WindowsSucks said:**
> Jasper now does text, I've modified my theme to fit.

The buttons on the side seem a bit silly to me (maybe on a widescreen monitor they'd make more sense). The program name being on the same line as the menu is awesome! How does that work? Is it just a simple overlay, or is it editing GTK stuff to make room?

---

### Post by klange on 2008-06-03
> The buttons on the side seem a bit silly to me (maybe on a widescreen monitor they'd make more sense). The program name being on the same line as the menu is awesome! How does that work? Is it just a simple overlay, or is it editing GTK stuff to make room?

Jasper can draw anywhere on a window (See the corners? Had to literally cut a hole out of them so that they would look right), so it was just a simple matter of finding a good font size that fit into the menu and writing up the theme. All standard monitors are wider than they are tall, so having buttons on the sides is almost always a more efficient use of screen space. I'll be moving window titles for inactive windows over there and making the buttons smaller as soon as I can.

---

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-06-04
> **rjmdomingo2003 said:**
> Maybe you could just comment-out (i.e. #) the line? Am not sure coz am still at v 2.1. Great set-up BTW!

Is that awesome logo (statusbar) part of the awesome package? Can't find it in google nor the website.
I think commenting it out just removes the tasklist from the statusbar.

The iconbox was in the default 2.3 setup:
```

         iconbox logo
         {
             image = "/usr/local/share/awesome/icons/awesome16.png"
             mouse
             {
                 button = "1"
                 command = "spawn"
                 arg = "exec xterm -e man awesome"
             }
         }


```

I changed the image and the command to launch thunar instead of xterm :)

---

### Post by PurposeOfReason on 2008-06-04
> **elmer_42 said:**
> PurposeOfReason, I always look forward to seeing your desktop. I have a question, though: Where did you get that awesome Mac-esque top bar?
That would be globalmenu2. If you're using Ubuntu there are straight .debs for it here.
[http://code.google.com/p/gnome2-globalmenu/](http://code.google.com/p/gnome2-globalmenu/)

On a side note, the webkit works still yet better, but you can't upload with it.

### Post by chucky chuckaluck on 2008-06-05
> **dbbolton said:**
> That Openbox theme looks somewhat familiar :-k

doh! forgot to mention it. my bad. it's, of course, the very fine [murrinaangustifolium](http://www.box-look.org/content/show.php/MurrinaAngustifolium?content=79448)

> Incidentally, could your post your .Xdefaults? I'm thinking of trying out urxvt.

```
urxvt*scrollBar: false
urxvt*foreground: gray90
urxvt*background: #000000
urxvt*font: xft:Nimbus Mono L-8
urxvt*cursorColor: green
urxvt*inheritPixmap: true
urxvt*geometry: 80x38
```

### Post by jakonj on 2008-06-05
ubuntu 8.04 + openbox 3.4 (without gnome or kde. just openbox ;) )

gtk2 theme: Murrina Neo Gilouche
wallpaper: one of many wallpapers from [http://www.vladstudio.com/](http://www.vladstudio.com/)
openbox theme: [GlossyBlue](http://www.box-look.org/content/show.php/GlossyBlue?content=79059)
icons: tango+[customized Discovery icons (only mimetypes)](http://jakonj.googlepages.com/mimetypes-svg.7z)
programs: rxvt-unicode, moc, [wbar](http://code.google.com/p/wbar/), conky, pypanel
font: Bitstream Vera Sans (size=8)


here is my moc theme:
[http://jakonj.googlepages.com/zlto](http://jakonj.googlepages.com/zlto)

i use this command to start rxvt-unicode with good transparency and good fonts:
```
rxvt -name rxvt -title 'Terminal :]' -sl 3000 -tr +sb -si -sk -fade 70 -sh 60 -fn -misc-fixed-medium-r-normal-*-*-120-*-*-c-*-iso8859-2 -g 77x27+20-0 -fg \#cecece
```

for war launching i use this command:
```
wbar -zoomf 1.001 -jumpf 0 -p bot-left -above-desk
```

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-06-05
> **HangukMiguk said:**
> If you'll pardon my asking, how does everyone get their theme details in terminal?
I do it by hand with an sh script:

```

#!/bin/sh
#Colors
blue="\033[1;34m"
green="\033[1;32m"
cyan="\033[1;36m"
red="\033[1;31m"
bblue="\033[0;38;5;12m"
orange="\033[0;38;5;130m"

#bold
bold="\033[00m"

#End
end="\033[0m"

echo " "
echo "\n"
echo $bblue" Ubuntu 7.04 $end"
echo " "
#echo $orange" Openbox:  $end Custom $end"
echo $orange" Gtk:      $end MurrinaAurantium"
echo $orange" Icons:    $end Crashbit"
echo $orange" Wall:     $end Oree"
echo "            astoyanov.deviantart.com"
echo $orange" Fonts:    $end Consolas, Myriad Web, nu"
#echo $orange" Apps:     $end Pidgin Screenlet, Pypanel "
#echo "           Quod Libet, Thunar, ttm "
echo " "
#date
echo " "
#scrot -d 10

```

This one should do it automatically, but only for GNOME:

```

#!/usr/bin/env bash

# screenshot dir
ssdir="$HOME/screenie/"
# screenshot description
ssdesc="$HOME/screenie"
# screenshot format
ss=`date +%d%m%Y`.png

#Couleurs
bleu="\033[1;34m"
cyan="\033[36m"
gris="\033[37m"

#Style
gras="\033[00m"

#Remise aux valeurs par défaut
fin="\033[0m"

# LINUX PART
echo
echo -e "$bleu LINUX $fin"

. /etc/lsb-release
echo -e "  Distro:        $gras $DISTRIB_ID $DISTRIB_RELEASE $DISTRIB_CODENAME$fin"
#echo -e "  Kernel:        $gras $(uname -r)$fin"
#echo -e "  Uptime:        $gras$(uptime |cut --delimiter=" " -f 4)$fin days and $gras$(uptime |cut --delimiter=" " -f 2)$fin hrs "


# HARDWARE PART
#echo
#echo -e "$bleu HARDWARE $fin"
#
#echo -e "  CPU:             $gras$(grep "model name" /proc/cpuinfo|cut --delimiter=":" -f 2 | head -n1| sed  -r "s/\s+/ /g")$fin " 
#echo -e "  GPU:              $gras$(cat /proc/driver/nvidia/cards/0 | grep Model | cut --delimiter=" " -f3,4,5,6,7,8,9)$fin"
#let memtotal=`grep "MemTotal" /proc/meminfo|cut -c 12-22|indent -i0`/1024
#echo -e "  RAM:              $gras$memtotal$fin mb"
#echo -e "  Bogomips:         $gras$(grep "bogomips" /proc/cpuinfo|cut --delimiter=":" -f 2 | head -n1)$fin bogomips"

 
# DESIGN PART
echo
echo -e  "$bleu DESIGN $fin"

echo -e "  Environment:        $gras Gnome$fin"
echo -e "  GTK2:            $gras $(gconftool-2 --get /desktop/gnome/interface/gtk_theme)$fin"
#echo -e "  Emerald:        $gras $(grep description $HOME/.emerald/theme/theme.ini |cut -c 13-)$fin"
echo -e "  Metacity:             $gras $(gconftool-2 --get /apps/metacity/general/theme)$fin"
echo -e "  Icons:        $gras $(gconftool-2 --get /desktop/gnome/interface/icon_theme)$fin"
echo -e "  Application Font:      $gras $(gconftool-2 --get /desktop/gnome/interface/font_name)$fin"
echo -e "  Terminal Font:    $gras $(gconftool-2 --get /apps/gnome-terminal/profiles/Default/font)$fin"
#echo -e "  Wallpaper:        $gras $(gconftool-2 --get /desktop/gnome/background/picture_filename | sed  -e "s,^.*/,," | cut --delimiter="." -f1)$fin"
#echo -e "  Resolution:        $gras $(xvidtune -show | cut --delimiter='"' -f2)$fin px"

#sleep 4
#scrot $ss
echo
exit 0

```

### Post by ayoli on 2008-06-06
> **schtufbox said:**
> Any chance you could upload your Eikon icon theme?
I've downloaded it twice now from different sites and each of them have the same problem...they make the panels huge due to no small icons.
like this:

I downloaded this pack from this url : [http://www.mediafire.com/?mh0tv32l42j](http://www.mediafire.com/?mh0tv32l42j)
Your issue can also come from the gtk theme. I have this line at the top of my theme gtkrc :
```
gtk-icon-sizes = "panel-menu=16,16:panel=16,16:gtk-button=16,16:gtk-large-toolbar=16,16"
```

---

### Post by schtufbox on 2008-06-06
> **ayoli said:**
> I downloaded this pack from this url : [http://www.mediafire.com/?mh0tv32l42j](http://www.mediafire.com/?mh0tv32l42j)
Your issue can also come from the gtk theme. I have this line at the top of my theme gtkrc :
```
gtk-icon-sizes = "panel-menu=16,16:panel=16,16:gtk-button=16,16:gtk-large-toolbar=16,16"
```
Thanks a lot :)

### Post by ad_267 on 2008-06-07
> **masterlotep said:**
> 
How did you embed the terminal with compiz is it a git plug in?

I followed this guide here: [http://icehot.wordpress.com/2008/05/11/ubuntu-hardy-tutorial-embed-terminal-into-your-desktop/](http://icehot.wordpress.com/2008/05/11/ubuntu-hardy-tutorial-embed-terminal-into-your-desktop/)
It uses the Window Rules plugin 

I launch it on startup with this:
gnome-terminal --window-with-profile=embedded --geometry 100x50+280+20

### Post by urukrama on 2008-06-08
> **aristotlewilde said:**
> 
I couldn't get a screenshot w/ the menu unfolded for the life of me!

You have to set a timer, so that you have enough time to open the desktop menu before the screenshot is taken. 

What do you use to take a screenshot? If you use scrot, use a command like "scrot -d 10" (for a delay of 10 seconds; see "man scrot" for more info); if you use the Gimp (File > Acquire) you can also specify a time delay. I'm not sure about the gnome screenshot app, as I haven't used that in ages, but I assume it has a similar function.

---

### Post by Ub1476 on 2008-06-09
```

               +             
               #             
              ###                OS: ArchLinux (Core Dump) 
             #####               Kernel: 2.6.25-ARCH 
             ######              WM: Openbox
            ; #####;             WM Theme: BlackWhite

### Post by trappy on 2008-06-10
> **OmniCloud said:**

For the wallpaper you might need something like i.e fe.

> **Yes said:**
> Very nice.  Mind sharing your .Xdefaults and .bashrc?

I can give you my .Xdefaults, but the terminal in the screenshot is gnome-terminal:
```

Xcursor.theme:Human
urxvt*scrollBar: false
urxvt*foreground: #ffffff
urxvt*background: #000000
urxvt*font: xft:Bitstream Vera Sans Mono-8.5
urxvt*cursorColor: orange
urxvt*inheritPixmap: false
urxvt*geometry: 75x15
urxvt*termName: xterm
urxvt*urllauncher: epiphany
urxvt*matcher.button: 
urxvt*saveLines: 1000 

```

And here is my .bashrc (it took me FOREVER to get these specific colors!):

```

# ~/.bashrc: executed by bash(1) for non-login shells.
# see /usr/share/doc/bash/examples/startup-files (in the package bash-doc)
# for examples

# If not running interactively, don't do anything
[ -z "$PS1" ] && return

# don't put duplicate lines in the history. See bash(1) for more options
export HISTCONTROL=ignoredups
# ... and ignore same sucessive entries.
export HISTCONTROL=ignoreboth

# check the window size after each command and, if necessary,
# update the values of LINES and COLUMNS.
#shopt -s checkwinsize

# make less more friendly for non-text input files, see lesspipe(1)
[ -x /usr/bin/lesspipe ] && eval "$(lesspipe)"

# set variable identifying the chroot you work in (used in the prompt below)
if [ -z "$debian_chroot" ] && [ -r /etc/debian_chroot ]; then
    debian_chroot=$(cat /etc/debian_chroot)
fi

# set a fancy prompt (non-color, unless we know we "want" color)
#case "$TERM" in
#xterm-color)
    
#PS1='${debian_chroot:+($debian_chroot)}\[\033[01;32m\]\u@\h\[\033[00m\]:\[\033[01;34m\]\w\[\033[00m\]\$ '
 #   ;;
#*)
#    PS1='\[\e[1;32m\][ ~ ] [1;37m\]'

#'${debian_chroot:+($debian_chroot)}\[\e[1;37m\]dbbolton[0;32m\][\W]\[\e[m\] '
    #PS1='${debian_chroot:+($debian_chroot)}\u@\h:\w\$ '
  #  ;;
#esac


#################################################
#
# HEADER
#
##################################


#export black="\[\033[0;38;5;0m\]"
#export red="\[\033[0;38;5;1m\]"
#export orange="\[\033[0;38;5;202m\]"
#export green="\[\033[0;38;5;2m\]"
#export yellow="\[\033[0;38;5;3m\]"
#export blue="\[\033[0;38;5;4m\]"
#export bblue="\[\033[0;38;5;12m\]"
#export magenta="\[\033[0;38;5;55m\]"
#export cyan="\[\033[0;38;5;6m\]"
#export white="\[\033[0;38;5;7m\]"
#export coldblue="\[\033[0;38;5;33m\]"
#export smoothblue="\[\033[0;38;5;111m\]"
#export iceblue="\[\033[0;38;5;45m\]"
#export turqoise="\[\033[0;38;5;50m\]"
#export smoothgreen="\[\033[0;38;5;42m\]"
#export end="\033[0m"

# Comment in the above and uncomment this below for a color prompt
#green
#PS1='${debian_chroot:+($debian_chroot)}\[\033[01;32m\]\[\033[00m\][\[\033[1;32m\] \w\[\033[00m\] ] '
#old one--- PS1='${debian_chroot:+($debian_chroot)}\[\033[01;32m\]\u@\h\[\033[00m\]:\[\033[01;34m\]\w\[\033[00m\]\$ '


PS1='\[\033[0;38;5;32m\][ \[\033[0;38;5;202m\]\w \[\033[0;38;5;32m\]] \033[0m'

# If this is an xterm set the title to user@host:dir
case "$TERM" in
xterm*|rxvt*)
    PROMPT_COMMAND='echo -ne "\033]0;${USER}@${HOSTNAME}: ${PWD/$HOME/~}\007"'
    ;;
*)
    ;;
esac

# Alias definitions.
# You may want to put all your additions into a separate file like
# ~/.bash_aliases, instead of adding them here directly.
# See /usr/share/doc/bash-doc/examples in the bash-doc package.

#if [ -f ~/.bash_aliases ]; then
#    . ~/.bash_aliases
#fi

# enable color support of ls and also add handy aliases
if [ "$TERM" != "dumb" ]; then
    eval "`dircolors -b`"
    alias ls='ls --color=auto'
    #alias dir='ls --color=auto --format=vertical'
    #alias vdir='ls --color=auto --format=long'
fi

# some more ls aliases
#alias ll='ls -l'
#alias la='ls -A'
#alias l='ls -CF'

# enable programmable completion features (you don't need to enable
# this, if it's already enabled in /etc/bash.bashrc and /etc/profile
# sources /etc/bash.bashrc).
if [ -f /etc/bash_completion ]; then
    . /etc/bash_completion
fi

```

### Post by lswest on 2008-06-11
Well, finally got Arch configured nicely with e17, so here's my desktop:
Wallpaper: War of the Depths (actually, each workspace has a different wallpaper, for a full list you can see the post on my blog of my artwork)

theme: Night-Bling from [here]("http://www1.get-e.org/Themes/E17/")

modules in the dock: bottom task (left to right): start;pager;ibox;ibar;temperature;cpu;wireless;battery;volume;screenshot;clock (using edjy theme on the clock)

top bar: itask ng

Second screenshot's running apps: XMMS;xterm (white terminal);sakura (black terminal); Eterm (terminal with background).  Still not sure which one I should use as default and customize :P any suggestions are welcome.

iconified apps: skype;pidgin;amsn;firefox3.

### Post by lswest on 2008-06-11
> **OmniCloud said:**
> That depends on what you mean by basic? I'll run down what I use my PC for in a quick roundup, and you tell me if that's basic or not k?

Web browsing/downloading music/video from various sources/chat w/Pidgin (Frostwire doesn't like my sun-java 6 for some reason though:confused:)
Converting with Winff so I can playback videos/anime on my PS3
Watchtower application relies on Wine
Media playback/Photos viewing & editing/tons of personalization;)

That about sums up what I do with Linux...Basic?

By basic I meant "default" I guess.  Basically, a basic system for me is one that isn't customized much, if at all.  And, so you know, if you install Arch using the core CD, you will have to install a Desktop Environment or a Window Manager, then install GNOME, etc. after installing the essentials like ALSA, xorg, etc. etc.  Basically, if you want a system that works well with little configuration, use Ubuntu or some other distro along those lines, or if you have time to spend configuring and installing applications that come pre-installed in Ubuntu, by all means, dual boot your ubuntu with Arch while you set it up and test it.  The main advantage in Arch is the AUR/ABS system (I find) and the customization that can give you a slight performance boost, as there are no excess programs running you don't need.  It also gives you a great understanding of how Linux works.  However, to answer your original question, I see those as "common" needs, not basic ones.  Lastly, more advanced would be if you intend to be compiling custom kernels, etc. etc. then Arch is definitely a good way to go with it's ABS and PKGBUILD system.

ABS=Arch Build System
AUR=Arch User Repository
PKGBUILD=file that contains instructions for compiling and creating .pkg.tar.gz files for pacman

---

### Post by Yes on 2008-06-11

.pypanelrc:

```
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
#
#                         PyPanel v2.4 Configuration
#
# This configuration file is a Python script that will be executed when
# PyPanel is started.  In order for PyPanel to start properly, make sure that
# this file contains proper Python formatting and no syntax errors.
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
VERSION         = 2.4           # Config file version

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Colors: Format is hex triplet - 0xrrggbb
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
#BG_COLOR        = "0xd6d6d6"    # Panel background and tinting color
#BG_COLOR	= "0x464646"
BG_COLOR	= "0x000000"
#TASK_COLOR      = "0x000000"    # Normal task name color 
TASK_COLOR	= "0xffffff"
FOCUSED_COLOR   = "0x620000"    # Focused task name color
SHADED_COLOR    = "0x5f5f5f"    # Shaded task name color 
#MINIMIZED_COLOR = "0x000000"    # Minimized task name color 
MINIMIZED_COLOR = "0xffffff"
#DESKTOP_COLOR   = "0x982f00"    # Desktop name color
DESKTOP_COLOR	= "0xff5f00"
CLOCK_COLOR     = "0x2621E3"    # Clock text color
LINE_COLOR      = "0x797979"    # Vertical line color

# Text Shadow Colors
TASK_SHADOW_COLOR      = "0xffffff"
FOCUSED_SHADOW_COLOR   = "0xffffff"
SHADED_SHADOW_COLOR    = "0xffffff"
MINIMIZED_SHADOW_COLOR = "0xffffff" 
DESKTOP_SHADOW_COLOR   = "0xffffff"
CLOCK_SHADOW_COLOR     = "0xffffff"

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Panel Spacing and Location Options: Measured in pixels
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
#P_LOCATION      = 1             # Panel placement: 0 = top, 1 = bottom
#P_WIDTH         = 0             # Panel width: 0 = Use full screen width
#P_START         = 5             # Starting X coordinate of the panel
#P_SPACER        = 6             # Spacing between panel objects
#P_HEIGHT        = 20            # Panel height
P_LOCATION    = 1        # panel placement: 0 = top, 1 = bottom
P_WIDTH        = 1300        # panel width: 0 = full screen width
P_START        = 70        # starting X coordinate of the panel
P_SPACER    = 15        # spacing between panel objects
P_HEIGHT    = 18 
P_L_BUFF        = 2
P_R_BUFF        = 2
P_T_BUFF        = 4
P_B_BUFF        = 40

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Icon Size Options: Measured in pixels
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
I_HEIGHT        = 16            # Panel application icon height
I_WIDTH         = 16            # Panel application icon Width 
APPL_I_HEIGHT   = 12            # Application launcher icon height
APPL_I_WIDTH    = 12            # Application launcher icon width
TRAY_I_HEIGHT   = 16            # System tray icon height (usually 16 or 24)
TRAY_I_WIDTH    = 16            # System tray icon width  (usually 16 or 24)
                                # If TRAY_I_WIDTH is set to 0, then the
                                # width specified by the tray app will be used
                                
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Panel Clock Format: 'man strftime' for detailed formatting options and help
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
CLOCK_FORMAT    = "%m-%d-%y %I:%M"    # Ex: 2004-09-25 17:45 

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Clock Delay: Seconds between each clock update during periods of inactivity
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
CLOCK_DELAY     = 20

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Hidden Application List: Apps listed here will not be display on the panel
# The application name is its WM_CLASS name, use 'xprop' to find WM_CLASS
# Ex: ["xmms", "xine", "gDesklets"]
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
HIDE_LIST       = []            
                   
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Hidden Panel Size: Size of the panel when it's hidden/minimized
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
HIDDEN_SIZE     = 2

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Panel Text Font: This option takes either a traditional or Xft font string 
# Ex: "-schumacher-clean-medium-r-normal-*-12-*-*-*-*-*-*-*"
#     "aquafont-8" 
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
FONT            = "nu"

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Show All Applications: Show apps from all desktops or just the current
# 0: Disabled - Only applications on the current desktop will be displayed
# 1: Enabled  - Selected apps are moved to the current desktop
# 2: Enabled  - Current desktop is changed to the selected apps desktop
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SHOWALL         = 2             # 0, 1 or 2 - see descriptions above

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Show Minimized/Iconified Applications: Show only minimized apps or all apps
# 0: Disabled - Show all applications on the panel
# 1: Enabled  - Show only minimized apps on the panel
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SHOWMINIMIZED   = 0

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Application Icon List: List of custom icons for specific applications
# The application name is its WM_CLASS name, use 'xprop' to find WM_CLASS
#
# The "default" entry is used for applications with no icon.  If left "",
# PyPanel will use the default icon distributed with the source.
#
# Add entries using the following format -
#     "<application name>" : "<full path to icon>",
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ICON_LIST       = {
                   "default" : "",
                   "example" : "/usr/share/imlib2/data/images/audio.png",
                  }
                  
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Application Launch List: Ordered list of icons and applications for the
#                          application launcher.
# 
# Add entries using the following format -
#     ("<executable>", "<full path to icon>")
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
LAUNCH_LIST     = [
		   #("", "/home/alex/Pictures/musicNote.png"),
		   #("mpc prev", "/home/alex/Pictures/prev.png"),
                   #("mpc toggle", "/home/alex/Pictures/pause.png"), 
		   #("mpc next", "/home/alex/Pictures/next.png")
                  ]

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Background Alpha/Shade Level: 0 (Fully Translucent) -> 255 (Fully Opaque)
# BG_COLOR is used for tinting
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SHADE           = 150

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Misc. Options: 1 = Enabled/Yes, 0 = Disabled/No
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ABOVE           = 1             # Panel is always above other apps
APPICONS        = 1             # Show application icons
AUTOHIDE        = 0             # Autohide uses the CLOCK_DELAY timer above
SHADOWS         = 0             # Show text shadows
SHOWLINES       = 0             # Show object seperation lines
SHOWBORDER      = 1             # Show a border around the panel

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Desktop Names: Configure the names of your desktops
# If the option is [], PyPanel will attempt to use the desktop name specified
# by the XServer, if that fails it will use the desktop number as its name
# Ex. ["One", "Two", "Three", "Four", "Five", "Six", "Seven", "Eight"]
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
DESKTOP_NAMES   = ["[ 1 ]", "[ 2 ]", "[ 3 ]", "[ 4 ]"]

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Panel Layout:       -----------------------------------
#                     [  1  ][  2  ][  3  ][  4  ][  5  ]
#                     -----------------------------------
#
# The panel layout is split into 5 sections numbered 1, 2, 3, 4 or 5 as shown
# in the diagram above.  Each of the following objects can be enabled by
# assigning it a section number or disabled by assigning it 0:
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
DESKTOP         = 1             # Desktop name section
TASKS           = 2             # Task names section 
TRAY            = 3             # System tray section
CLOCK           = 5             # Clock section
LAUNCHER        = 0             # Application launcher section

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
#                       Button Event Function Definitions
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Left click   - button 1 
# Middle click - button 2
# Right click  - button 3
# Wheel up     - button 4
# Wheel down   - button 5 
#
# changeDesktop(x)
# - Change Desktop: Increase or decrease the current desktop by 'x' amount
# 
# toggleShade(task)
# - Shade or Unshade an application
#
# toggleHidden()
# - Minimize the panel to the top or bottom depending on its start location
#
# toggleMinimize(task, traise=1)
# - Minimize or Unminimize an application and optionally raise it
#
# taskRaise(task, focus=1)
# - Raise an application to the top of the window list and optionally focus it 
#
# taskLower(task, focus=0)
# - Lower an app to the bottom of the window list and optionally focus it
#
# taskFocus(task)
# - Give focus to the selected application, if it has focus then minimize it
#
# showDesktop()
# - Toggle between hiding and unhiding ALL applications
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#----------------------------------
def desktopButtonEvent(pp, button):
#----------------------------------
    """ Button event handler for the panel's desktop object """
        
    if button == 1:
        pp.changeDesktop(-1)
    elif button == 2:
        #pp.changeDesktop(2)
        pp.showDesktop ()
    elif button == 3:
        pp.changeDesktop(1)
    elif button == 4:
        pp.changeDesktop(1)
    elif button == 5:
        pp.changeDesktop(-1)
        
#--------------------------------
def clockButtonEvent(pp, button):
#--------------------------------
    """ Button event handler for the panel's clock object """
    
    if button == 1:
        os.system("xclock &")
    elif button == 2:
        pass
    elif button == 3:
        pp.toggleHidden()  
    elif button == 4:
        pp.showDesktop()
    elif button == 5:
        pp.showDesktop()
        
#--------------------------------
def panelButtonEvent(pp, button):
#--------------------------------
    """ Button event handler for the panel with no active tasks """
    
    if button == 1:
        pass
    elif button == 2:
        pass
    elif button == 3:
        pass
    elif button == 4:
        pass
    elif button == 5:
        pass
        
#-------------------------------------
def taskButtonEvent(pp, button, task):
#-------------------------------------
    """ Button event handler for the panel's tasks """
    
    if button == 1:
        pp.taskFocus(task)
    elif button == 2:
        # Destroy the application
        task.obj.destroy()
    elif button == 3:
        # Ex. - XMMS doesn't shade, so we want to minimize it instead and
        #       still use button 3 to shade other applications
        #       task.tclass is the tasks class name (WM_CLASS)
        if "xmms" in task.tclass:
            pp.toggleMinimize(task)
        else:
            pp.toggleShade(task)
    elif button == 4:
        pp.taskRaise(task, focus=1)
    elif button == 5:
        pp.taskLower(task, focus=0)
        
```

.conkyrc:

```

# set to yes if you want Conky to be forked in the background
# make conky its own window
own_window yes
own_window_type desktop
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,sticky,below,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
background no

# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# fiddle with window
use_spacer none
use_xft yes

# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 3.0


# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Text stuff
draw_outline no # amplifies text if yes
draw_borders no

uppercase no # set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase

draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders yes
stippled_borders 0
border_margin 3
border_width 0

# Default colors and also border colors, grey90 == #e5e5e5
color1 680000
default_color 000000
own_window_colour 000000

# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
alignment top_left
#alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_right

# Gap between borders of screen and text
gap_x 300
gap_y 10

minimum_size 10 5

override_utf8_locale no
xftfont AvantGarde LT Medium-8
xftalpha 0.8

text_buffer_size 2048

TEXT
Arch: $color1$kernel $color| Up: $color1$uptime $color| CPU: ${Freq_dyn} MHz 1: $color1${cpu cp1}% ${color}2: $color1${cpu cpu2}% $color| RAM: $color1$mem $memperc% $color| / $color1${fs_used /} ${fs_used_perc /}% $color/data$color1 ${fs_used /home/alex/data} ${fs_used_perc /home/alex/data}% $color| Down: $color1${downspeed eth0} k/s $color| UpS: $color1${upspeed eth0} k/s $color| Mail: $color1${execi 300 gmail}
```

How'd you get the submenu to float off of the main popmenu?

---

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-06-12
> **Yes said:**
> How'd you get the submenu to float off of the main popmenu?

I really like that GTK theme :)

Thanks. 

It's easy to do. Just put this in your themerc:

```

menu.overlap: -3

```The more negative, the farther away the submenu is, and positive makes it overlap the parent menu.

---

### Post by Yes on 2008-06-12
Thanks!

### Post by RiceMonster on 2008-06-12
> **urukrama said:**
> Not very hard. Follow the link in my signature for help.

Your guide is superior. I use it whenever I want to know anything about Openbox. I found it more useful than the official Openbox documentation.

[quote=Arlanthir]There goes my

    sudo apt-get install openbox-logout-login-choose theme 

dream =X

Thank you, I'll probably give it a go when I get the time =)[/quote]

It does take a little time at first, but that's basically just learning how to switch from a DE to a WM. It took me a little bit to get it how I wanted it, but that was basically finding out what tools I needed and the like. The config files are in XML which I really like, and you use a shell script to autostart programs. That's really easy though. All you need to do to have start on login is add a line like "command for program &". If you give it a chance, you'll find it extremely customizable.

---

### Post by nabl on 2008-06-13
I finished this setup earlier today. Here you go:

Clean:
[[IMG]http://img526.imageshack.us/img526/6206/blackandgreenfd9.th.jpg[/IMG]]("http://img526.imageshack.us/img526/6206/blackandgreenfd9.jpg")

Busy:
[[IMG]http://img249.imageshack.us/img249/4716/blackandgreenbusybq2.th.jpg[/IMG]]("http://img249.imageshack.us/img249/4716/blackandgreenbusybq2.jpg")

And here's some information. There are quite a few custom modifications; if you want any, just ask. ;)

  OS: ArchLinux 
  WM: Openbox
  WM Theme: Mire_v2.5_green  <-- This is my modification of the Mire_v2_lime Openbox theme.
  Icons: green-tango   <-- I made this with Tango Generator; it's mainly the green recoloring of the official Tango theme.
  Font: Bitstream Vera Sans 9
  GTK Theme: Nodoka-Midnight-Green  <-- This is my modification of the Nodoka-Midnight theme. I just changed the blues to green.
Panel: pypanel with a custom theme to match everything else.
Background: It is from InterfaceLift. [Here's a link.]("http://interfacelift.com/wallpaper/details.php?id=1599")

Overall, I'm really enjoying this theme; it's my favorite dark theme yet. :)

### Post by rjmdomingo2003 on 2008-06-14
> **Chokkan said:**
> So is it possible to have  desktop icons without titles below them (and even without any highlighting) under Gnome?
Under Gnome, I doubt, coz it's already a desktop environment (i.e. with icons). With Awesome, which is a window manager only, you'd need idesk: [http://idesk.sourceforge.net/wiki/index.php/Idesk-usage](http://idesk.sourceforge.net/wiki/index.php/Idesk-usage)

Can you post your .bashrc for how you got your prompt like that?

---

### Post by Alasdair on 2008-06-14
That's zsh, not bash. Here's the relevant part of my .zshrc anyway, maybe you'll be able to translate it for your .bashrc.
```

## Load colors
autoload colors zsh/terminfo
if [[ "$terminfo[colors]" -ge 8 ]]; then
    colors
fi
for color in RED GREEN YELLOW BLUE MAGENTA CYAN WHITE; do
    eval PR_B_$color='%{$terminfo[bold]$fg[${(L)color}]%}'
    eval PR_$color='%{$fg[${(L)color}]%}'
    (( count = $count + 1 ))
done
PR_NO_COLOR="%{$terminfo[sgr0]%}"

## prompt 
PROMPT="$PR_CYAN&#9484;&#9472;&#9472;&#9472;&#9508;${PR_B_CYAN}\
[$PR_NO_COLOR%l$PR_B_CYAN]\
[$PR_NO_COLOR%/$PR_B_CYAN]
$PR_CYAN&#9492;&#9472;&#9508;$PR_NO_COLOR "

```

---

### Post by ad_267 on 2008-06-15
> **blackvd said:**
> How do you get your gnome-panel transparent?

You right click on the panel and select properties. Select the background tab. Set it to solid colour and decrease the opacity down to 0.

---

### Post by blackvd on 2008-06-15

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-06-17
> **rjmdomingo2003 said:**
> Nice polish, as always!
Thanks!

> **Happy_Man said:**
> What icons are you using?
Check the terminal ;) They're called Nou or Dropline Nou. You can get them here:
[http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Dropline+NOU%21?content=53292](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Dropline+NOU%21?content=53292)


> **trappy said:**
> Where can I find that themeinfo python script? :)
You can get the script as well as usage notes about it here: [http://danielsudo.blogspot.com/2008/06/openbox-theme-info-script.html](http://danielsudo.blogspot.com/2008/06/openbox-theme-info-script.html)

I'm still working on it, so if you find any problems, please leave a comment on my blog :)

### Post by denham2010 on 2008-06-21
> Originally posted by **trappy**
@ denham2010: I've been looking for some decent audio visualizations for linux, but I haven't found nothing yet. ProjectM does, however, look good, though I've no idea how to install it. Can you guide me please? Also, I'm using moc, is it possible to use ProjectM with that? The Pulseaudio version maybe?

Following are the instructions I used to install ProjectM-pulseaudio from SVN. If you need a different version, visit [ProjectM]("http://sourceforge.net/projects/projectm/") where you can download all the different packages.

Install dependencies
```
sudo apt-get install libglew1.5 libglew1.5-dev ftgl-dev libpulse-dev subversion cmake libvisual-0.4-dev libsdl-dev libqt4-dev build-essential
```

Download the latest trunk from SVN
```
cd ~
mkdir projectm
cd projectm
svn co https://projectm.svn.sf.net/svnroot/projectm/trunk projectM-Trunk
```

Configure
```
cd projectM-Trunk/src
ccmake .
```

**NOTE:** See the '.' above? That's important! You must include it in your command or it won't work.

Now cmake will load. Press "c" to configure projectM. Highlight the CMAKE_BUILD_TYPE field, press enter and type "Release" there. Press enter again. Then highlight the CMAKE_INSTALL_PREFIX field and change /usr/local to /usr/. Then press "c" again to configure it with those parameters.

**NOTE:** If you run into dependency problems when trying to configure cmake, it can usually be solved by doing "rm CMakeCache.txt" in the src directory.

Now that cmake has got it's configuration right, press "g" to generate a makefile and exit.

Make and install
```
make && sudo make install
```

Once installed, keep the install folder on your computer incase you wish to remove ProjectM.

To remove
```
cd ~/projectm
sudo make uninstall
```

There is a lot of active development going on with ProjectM, so if you are having problems with the version downloaded, keep an eye on the sourceforge page (link above) for updates to trunk, and then try installing again.

Thanks to the following link which is where I got my install instructions. You may also want to keep tabs on this thread as it will most likely be updated as changes are made to ProjectM.

[URL="http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=749793"]
Ubuntu Forums ProjectM How To[/URL]

Cheers.

---

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-06-23
> **PrimoTurbo said:**
> Love your desktops.

I have a few questions.. 

What taskbar/dock are you using? Are the little indents part of it or are they a wallpaper tricks?

You don't seem to have min/max/close buttons? How do you manage the windows with shortcuts?

Thanks. The panel at the bottom is pypanel. The background is just a wallpaper trick. 

I actually do have those buttons, but they only appear when the mouse moves over them. It's possible to go without window decorations in Openbox:

Alt+F4 = close
Alt+Space = show menu
Alt+ Left Click & drag = move
Alt + Right click & drag = resize

These are the default bindings. I suppose you could add some for iconify/minimize and maximize.

> **etnlIcarus said:**
> If you don't mind holding my hand a little further, you wouldn't be able to tell me how you got the artwiz fonts working, would you? I've downloaded the xfonts-artwiz package from Gutsy. When that didn't result in the fonts becoming available, I put the cure fonts in my .fonts folder and followed the instructions on the Fluxbox wiki yet, after reloading the font cache and restarting X, my apps still don't seem to be able to detect the fonts.
Pardon the intrusion, but you have to enable bitmapped fonts. By default, it's turned off. Run 
```
sudo dpkg-reconfigure fontconfig-config
```
And turn it on :)

### Post by isaacj87 on 2008-06-24
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Just out of curiosity, how thin can you make the panel in 4.1?
Giant panels piss me off. They're such a waste of space.

In the later releases of KDE4, you can right click the panel, choose "Panel settings" (or something close to that) and set a custom pixel height. In KDE 4.1 beta, they've got this weird bar thing you can adjust to make the panel bigger or smaller...I'm not very particular to it.

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-06-25
> **PrimoTurbo said:**
> More hacks with pypanel, I wonder if anyone figures out how I gave it a skin and a start button.

[[IMG]http://img79.imageshack.us/img79/2272/200806250832461280x1024ys5.th.png[/IMG]](http://img79.imageshack.us/my.php?image=200806250832461280x1024ys5.png)
It looks great. If I understand correctly, your menu button is part of your wallpaper? Another way to make a start button is to specify the image with the launcher (in the LAUNCH_LIST section) and then specify the icon's size with the "APPL_I_HEIGHT" and "APPL_I_WIDTH" parameters.

---

### Post by PrimoTurbo on 2008-06-25
> **dbbolton said:**
> It looks great. If I understand correctly, your menu button is part of your wallpaper? Another way to make a start button is to specify the image with the launcher (in the LAUNCH_LIST section) and then specify the icon's size with the "APPL_I_HEIGHT" and "APPL_I_WIDTH" parameters.

Thanks, unfortunately I use that method already to position the volume icon. But yes the menu button is blank wallpaper so I can right click on it if I am in a full screen application.

---

### Post by urukrama on 2008-06-25
> **PrimoTurbo said:**
> 
I was just reading your ideas about xautolock, i have a menu on the left bottom when i however for a second. But ultimately not the best solution I'll probably implement something else to get a cool start button/menu.

You could use the desktop name section for this. Just set the font colour of the desktop name (DESKTOP_COLOR) to the colour of your menu icon so it remains invisible. 

At the bottom of your pypanelrc, have something like this instead of the default desktopButtonEvent section:

```
#----------------------------------
def desktopButtonEvent(pp, button):
#----------------------------------
    """ Button event handler for the panel's desktop object """
        
    if button == 1:
       **os.system("xte 'key Pause' &")**
    elif button == 2:
        pp.showDesktop()
    elif button == 3:
        pp.changeDesktop(-1)
    elif button == 4:
        pp.changeDesktop(1)
    elif button == 5:
        pp.changeDesktop(-1)
```

Xte is part of [xautomation]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/hardy/xautomation"). Make sure you specify in your rc.xml that your root menu is launched with whatever key you specified above (in this example "Pause Break"). You cannot use modifiers (Alt, Ctrl, etc.) with xte. Instead of xte, you could also use [xdotool]("http://www.semicomplete.com/projects/xdotool/").

If you want to launch the menu with a right click, add the line that is bold to just after the "button == 3" line instead.

> **PrimoTurbo said:**
> Your guides are great btw.

Thank you :D

### Post by PrimoTurbo on 2008-06-25
> **DarkDemonNT said:**
> I like this bar.
How can i take this bar?
Thank you.

It's just conky and the rest is part of the wallpaper.

Setup your conky in a similar way. Then make a selection on your wallpaper and light gradient it from bottom, and left and right. I also added a faint border. Essentially it's a fake effect and not a real bar, but looks cool and uses very little resources.

### Post by PrimoTurbo on 2008-06-25
> **urukrama said:**
> You could use the desktop name section for this. Just set the font colour of the desktop name (DESKTOP_COLOR) to the colour of your menu icon so it remains invisible. 

At the bottom of your pypanelrc, have something like this instead of the default desktopButtonEvent section:

```
#----------------------------------
def desktopButtonEvent(pp, button):
#----------------------------------
    """ Button event handler for the panel's desktop object """
        
    if button == 1:
       **os.system("xte 'key Pause' &")**
    elif button == 2:
        pp.showDesktop()
    elif button == 3:
        pp.changeDesktop(-1)
    elif button == 4:
        pp.changeDesktop(1)
    elif button == 5:
        pp.changeDesktop(-1)
```

Xte is part of [xautomation]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/hardy/xautomation"). Make sure you specify in your rc.xml that your root menu is launched with whatever key you specified above (in this example "Pause Break"). You cannot use modifiers (Alt, Ctrl, etc.) with xte. Instead of xte, you could also use [xdotool]("http://www.semicomplete.com/projects/xdotool/").

If you want to launch the menu with a right click, add the line that is bold to just after the "button == 3" line instead.



Thank you :D

Excellent idea thanks.

**EDIT:** Yeah just implemented it, even better you can name the desktops with spaces!!! So it's an awesome fake start button.

### Post by Yes on 2008-06-25
> **Opeth115 said:**
> would u mind posting ur pypanel rc?

Sure - 

```
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
#
#                         PyPanel v2.4 Configuration
#
# This configuration file is a Python script that will be executed when
# PyPanel is started.  In order for PyPanel to start properly, make sure that
# this file contains proper Python formatting and no syntax errors.
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
VERSION         = 2.4           # Config file version

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Colors: Format is hex triplet - 0xrrggbb
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
#BG_COLOR        = "0xd6d6d6"    # Panel background and tinting color
#BG_COLOR	= "0x464646"
BG_COLOR	= "0x000000"
#TASK_COLOR      = "0x000000"    # Normal task name color 
TASK_COLOR	= "0xffffff"
FOCUSED_COLOR   = "0x620000"    # Focused task name color
SHADED_COLOR    = "0x5f5f5f"    # Shaded task name color 
#MINIMIZED_COLOR = "0x000000"    # Minimized task name color 
MINIMIZED_COLOR = "0xffffff"
#DESKTOP_COLOR   = "0x982f00"    # Desktop name color
DESKTOP_COLOR	= "0xff5f00"
CLOCK_COLOR     = "0x2621E3"    # Clock text color
LINE_COLOR      = "0x797979"    # Vertical line color

# Text Shadow Colors
TASK_SHADOW_COLOR      = "0xffffff"
FOCUSED_SHADOW_COLOR   = "0xffffff"
SHADED_SHADOW_COLOR    = "0xffffff"
MINIMIZED_SHADOW_COLOR = "0xffffff" 
DESKTOP_SHADOW_COLOR   = "0xffffff"
CLOCK_SHADOW_COLOR     = "0xffffff"

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Panel Spacing and Location Options: Measured in pixels
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
#P_LOCATION      = 1             # Panel placement: 0 = top, 1 = bottom
#P_WIDTH         = 0             # Panel width: 0 = Use full screen width
#P_START         = 5             # Starting X coordinate of the panel
#P_SPACER        = 6             # Spacing between panel objects
#P_HEIGHT        = 20            # Panel height
P_LOCATION    = 1        # panel placement: 0 = top, 1 = bottom
P_WIDTH        = 1300        # panel width: 0 = full screen width
P_START        = 70        # starting X coordinate of the panel
P_SPACER    = 15        # spacing between panel objects
P_HEIGHT    = 18 
P_L_BUFF        = 2
P_R_BUFF        = 2
P_T_BUFF        = 4
P_B_BUFF        = 40

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Icon Size Options: Measured in pixels
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
I_HEIGHT        = 16            # Panel application icon height
I_WIDTH         = 16            # Panel application icon Width 
APPL_I_HEIGHT   = 12            # Application launcher icon height
APPL_I_WIDTH    = 12            # Application launcher icon width
TRAY_I_HEIGHT   = 16            # System tray icon height (usually 16 or 24)
TRAY_I_WIDTH    = 16            # System tray icon width  (usually 16 or 24)
                                # If TRAY_I_WIDTH is set to 0, then the
                                # width specified by the tray app will be used
                                
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Panel Clock Format: 'man strftime' for detailed formatting options and help
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
CLOCK_FORMAT    = "%m-%d-%y %I:%M"    # Ex: 2004-09-25 17:45 

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Clock Delay: Seconds between each clock update during periods of inactivity
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
CLOCK_DELAY     = 20

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Hidden Application List: Apps listed here will not be display on the panel
# The application name is its WM_CLASS name, use 'xprop' to find WM_CLASS
# Ex: ["xmms", "xine", "gDesklets"]
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
HIDE_LIST       = []            
                   
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Hidden Panel Size: Size of the panel when it's hidden/minimized
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
HIDDEN_SIZE     = 2

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Panel Text Font: This option takes either a traditional or Xft font string 
# Ex: "-schumacher-clean-medium-r-normal-*-12-*-*-*-*-*-*-*"
#     "aquafont-8" 
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
FONT            = "nu"

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Show All Applications: Show apps from all desktops or just the current
# 0: Disabled - Only applications on the current desktop will be displayed
# 1: Enabled  - Selected apps are moved to the current desktop
# 2: Enabled  - Current desktop is changed to the selected apps desktop
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SHOWALL         = 2             # 0, 1 or 2 - see descriptions above

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Show Minimized/Iconified Applications: Show only minimized apps or all apps
# 0: Disabled - Show all applications on the panel
# 1: Enabled  - Show only minimized apps on the panel
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SHOWMINIMIZED   = 0

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Application Icon List: List of custom icons for specific applications
# The application name is its WM_CLASS name, use 'xprop' to find WM_CLASS
#
# The "default" entry is used for applications with no icon.  If left "",
# PyPanel will use the default icon distributed with the source.
#
# Add entries using the following format -
#     "<application name>" : "<full path to icon>",
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ICON_LIST       = {
                   "default" : "",
                   "example" : "/usr/share/imlib2/data/images/audio.png",
                  }
                  
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Application Launch List: Ordered list of icons and applications for the
#                          application launcher.
# 
# Add entries using the following format -
#     ("<executable>", "<full path to icon>")
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
LAUNCH_LIST     = [
		   #("", "/home/alex/Pictures/musicNote.png"),
		   #("mpc prev", "/home/alex/Pictures/prev.png"),
                   #("mpc toggle", "/home/alex/Pictures/pause.png"), 
		   #("mpc next", "/home/alex/Pictures/next.png")
                  ]

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Background Alpha/Shade Level: 0 (Fully Translucent) -> 255 (Fully Opaque)
# BG_COLOR is used for tinting
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SHADE           = 150

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Misc. Options: 1 = Enabled/Yes, 0 = Disabled/No
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ABOVE           = 1             # Panel is always above other apps
APPICONS        = 0             # Show application icons
AUTOHIDE        = 0             # Autohide uses the CLOCK_DELAY timer above
SHADOWS         = 0             # Show text shadows
SHOWLINES       = 0             # Show object seperation lines
SHOWBORDER      = 1             # Show a border around the panel

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Desktop Names: Configure the names of your desktops
# If the option is [], PyPanel will attempt to use the desktop name specified
# by the XServer, if that fails it will use the desktop number as its name
# Ex. ["One", "Two", "Three", "Four", "Five", "Six", "Seven", "Eight"]
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
DESKTOP_NAMES   = ["[ 1 ]", "[ 2 ]", "[ 3 ]", "[ 4 ]"]

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Panel Layout:       -----------------------------------
#                     [  1  ][  2  ][  3  ][  4  ][  5  ]
#                     -----------------------------------
#
# The panel layout is split into 5 sections numbered 1, 2, 3, 4 or 5 as shown
# in the diagram above.  Each of the following objects can be enabled by
# assigning it a section number or disabled by assigning it 0:
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
DESKTOP         = 1             # Desktop name section
TASKS           = 2             # Task names section 
TRAY            = 3             # System tray section
CLOCK           = 5             # Clock section
LAUNCHER        = 0             # Application launcher section

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
#                       Button Event Function Definitions
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Left click   - button 1 
# Middle click - button 2
# Right click  - button 3
# Wheel up     - button 4
# Wheel down   - button 5 
#
# changeDesktop(x)
# - Change Desktop: Increase or decrease the current desktop by 'x' amount
# 
# toggleShade(task)
# - Shade or Unshade an application
#
# toggleHidden()
# - Minimize the panel to the top or bottom depending on its start location
#
# toggleMinimize(task, traise=1)
# - Minimize or Unminimize an application and optionally raise it
#
# taskRaise(task, focus=1)
# - Raise an application to the top of the window list and optionally focus it 
#
# taskLower(task, focus=0)
# - Lower an app to the bottom of the window list and optionally focus it
#
# taskFocus(task)
# - Give focus to the selected application, if it has focus then minimize it
#
# showDesktop()
# - Toggle between hiding and unhiding ALL applications
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#----------------------------------
def desktopButtonEvent(pp, button):
#----------------------------------
    """ Button event handler for the panel's desktop object """
        
    if button == 1:
        pp.changeDesktop(-1)
    elif button == 2:
        #pp.changeDesktop(2)
        pp.showDesktop ()
    elif button == 3:
        pp.changeDesktop(1)
    elif button == 4:
        pp.changeDesktop(1)
    elif button == 5:
        pp.changeDesktop(-1)
        
#--------------------------------
def clockButtonEvent(pp, button):
#--------------------------------
    """ Button event handler for the panel's clock object """
    
    if button == 1:
        os.system("xclock &")
    elif button == 2:
        pass
    elif button == 3:
        pp.toggleHidden()  
    elif button == 4:
        pp.showDesktop()
    elif button == 5:
        pp.showDesktop()
        
#--------------------------------
def panelButtonEvent(pp, button):
#--------------------------------
    """ Button event handler for the panel with no active tasks """
    
    if button == 1:
        pass
    elif button == 2:
        pass
    elif button == 3:
        pass
    elif button == 4:
        pass
    elif button == 5:
        pass
        
#-------------------------------------
def taskButtonEvent(pp, button, task):
#-------------------------------------
    """ Button event handler for the panel's tasks """
    
    if button == 1:
        pp.taskFocus(task)
    elif button == 2:
        # Destroy the application
        task.obj.destroy()
    elif button == 3:
        # Ex. - XMMS doesn't shade, so we want to minimize it instead and
        #       still use button 3 to shade other applications
        #       task.tclass is the tasks class name (WM_CLASS)
        if "xmms" in task.tclass:
            pp.toggleMinimize(task)
        else:
            pp.toggleShade(task)
    elif button == 4:
        pp.taskRaise(task, focus=1)
    elif button == 5:
        pp.taskLower(task, focus=0)
```

### Post by urukrama on 2008-06-26
> **dbbolton said:**
> After benchmarking a few different GTK engines, I was surprised to see how fast Clearlooks is, so I have been using it more often. Mist is marginally faster, but I think Clearlooks is much more aesthetically appealing.

My current favourite engine is the Xfce engine. According to [this test]("http://gianvito.wordpress.com/2008/02/20/gtk-engines-benchmarks-whats-the-fastest/4/") it is also the fastest.

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-06-26
> **PrimoTurbo said:**
> I remember I found a link one time which showed various statistic about engines, yes clearlooks, mist and murrina were at the top. Nice desktop btw.

What menu do you use? I'm assuming you are using pypanel launcher section for the menu?

Thanks. It's a launcher for the Openbox menu. This article will show you how to get a command to launch it: [http://crunchbang.org/archives/2008/03/14/invoke-openboxs-menu-with-xdotool/](http://crunchbang.org/archives/2008/03/14/invoke-openboxs-menu-with-xdotool/)

> **urukrama said:**
> My current favourite engine is the Xfce engine. According to [this test]("http://gianvito.wordpress.com/2008/02/20/gtk-engines-benchmarks-whats-the-fastest/4/") it is also the fastest.

The problem I have with this test is that it looks like only one trial was done for each engine. Benchmarking is tough in general, and there are a lot of parameters to consider with Gtk engines. For example, I've noticed that changing theme properties can affect the time, as well as the interface font.

---

### Post by elmer_42 on 2008-06-27
> **myusername said:**
> would you mind posting your pypanelrc?
No, I wouldn't. If I remember correctly it's only a small modification of the original .pypanelrc.
```
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
#
#                         PyPanel v2.4 Configuration
#
# This configuration file is a Python script that will be executed when
# PyPanel is started.  In order for PyPanel to start properly, make sure that
# this file contains proper Python formatting and no syntax errors.
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
VERSION         = 2.4           # Config file version

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Colors: Format is hex triplet - 0xrrggbb
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
BG_COLOR        = "0xFFFFFF"    # Panel background and tinting color
TASK_COLOR      = "0xe6e6e6"    # Normal task name color 
FOCUSED_COLOR   = "0x5fb2d6"    # Focused task name color
SHADED_COLOR    = "0x808080"    # Shaded task name color 
MINIMIZED_COLOR = "0x808080"    # Minimized task name color 
DESKTOP_COLOR   = "0xe6e6e6"    # Desktop name color
CLOCK_COLOR     = "0xe6e6e6"    # Clock text color
LINE_COLOR      = "0x606060"    # Vertical line color

# Text Shadow Colors
TASK_SHADOW_COLOR      = "0xffffff"
FOCUSED_SHADOW_COLOR   = "0xffffff"
SHADED_SHADOW_COLOR    = "0xffffff"
MINIMIZED_SHADOW_COLOR = "0xffffff" 
DESKTOP_SHADOW_COLOR   = "0xffffff"
CLOCK_SHADOW_COLOR     = "0xffffff"

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Panel Spacing and Location Options: Measured in pixels
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
P_LOCATION      = 1             # Panel placement: 0 = top, 1 = bottom
P_WIDTH         = 0             # Panel width: 0 = Use full screen width
P_START         = 0             # Starting X coordinate of the panel
P_SPACER        = 6             # Spacing between panel objects
P_HEIGHT        = 22            # Panel height

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Icon Size Options: Measured in pixels
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
I_HEIGHT        = 16            # Panel application icon height
I_WIDTH         = 16            # Panel application icon Width 
APPL_I_HEIGHT   = 24            # Application launcher icon height
APPL_I_WIDTH    = 24            # Application launcher icon width
TRAY_I_HEIGHT   = 24            # System tray icon height (usually 16 or 24)
TRAY_I_WIDTH    = 24            # System tray icon width  (usually 16 or 24)
                                # If TRAY_I_WIDTH is set to 0, then the
                                # width specified by the tray app will be used
                                
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Panel Clock Format: 'man strftime' for detailed formatting options and help
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
CLOCK_FORMAT    = "%m.%d.%y %H:%M:%S" 

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Clock Delay: Seconds between each clock update during periods of inactivity
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
CLOCK_DELAY     = 20

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Hidden Application List: Apps listed here will not be display on the panel
# The application name is its WM_CLASS name, use 'xprop' to find WM_CLASS
# Ex: ["xmms", "xine", "gDesklets"]
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
HIDE_LIST       = []            
                   
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Hidden Panel Size: Size of the panel when it's hidden/minimized
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
HIDDEN_SIZE     = 2

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Panel Text Font: This option takes either a traditional or Xft font string 
# Ex: "-schumacher-clean-medium-r-normal-*-12-*-*-*-*-*-*-*"
#     "aquafont-8" 
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
FONT            = "Cicle Fina-8"

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Show All Applications: Show apps from all desktops or just the current
# 0: Disabled - Only applications on the current desktop will be displayed
# 1: Enabled  - Selected apps are moved to the current desktop
# 2: Enabled  - Current desktop is changed to the selected apps desktop
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SHOWALL         = 0             # 0, 1 or 2 - see descriptions above

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Show Minimized/Iconified Applications: Show only minimized apps or all apps
# 0: Disabled - Show all applications on the panel
# 1: Enabled  - Show only minimized apps on the panel
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SHOWMINIMIZED   = 0

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Application Icon List: List of custom icons for specific applications
# The application name is its WM_CLASS name, use 'xprop' to find WM_CLASS
#
# The "default" entry is used for applications with no icon.  If left "",
# PyPanel will use the default icon distributed with the source.
#
# Add entries using the following format -
#     "<application name>" : "<full path to icon>",
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ICON_LIST       = {
                   "default" : "",
                   "example" : "/usr/share/imlib2/data/images/audio.png",
                  }
                  
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Application Launch List: Ordered list of icons and applications for the
#                          application launcher.
# 
# Add entries using the following format -
#     ("<executable>", "<full path to icon>")
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
LAUNCH_LIST     = [
                   ("gimp-2.2", "/usr/share/imlib2/data/images/paper.png"), 
                  ]

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Background Alpha/Shade Level: 0 (Fully Translucent) -> 255 (Fully Opaque)
# BG_COLOR is used for tinting
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SHADE           = 64

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Misc. Options: 1 = Enabled/Yes, 0 = Disabled/No
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ABOVE           = 1             # Panel is always above other apps
APPICONS        = 1             # Show application icons
AUTOHIDE        = 0             # Autohide uses the CLOCK_DELAY timer above
SHADOWS         = 0             # Show text shadows
SHOWLINES       = 0             # Show object seperation lines
SHOWBORDER      = 0             # Show a border around the panel

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Desktop Names: Configure the names of your desktops
# If the option is [], PyPanel will attempt to use the desktop name specified
# by the XServer, if that fails it will use the desktop number as its name
# Ex. ["One", "Two", "Three", "Four", "Five", "Six", "Seven", "Eight"]
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
DESKTOP_NAMES   = ["one", "two", "three", "four"]

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Panel Layout:       -----------------------------------
#                     [  1  ][  2  ][  3  ][  4  ][  5  ]
#                     -----------------------------------
#
# The panel layout is split into 5 sections numbered 1, 2, 3, 4 or 5 as shown
# in the diagram above.  Each of the following objects can be enabled by
# assigning it a section number or disabled by assigning it 0:
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
DESKTOP         = 1             # Desktop name section
TASKS           = 2             # Task names section 
TRAY            = 3             # System tray section
CLOCK           = 4             # Clock section
LAUNCHER        = 0             # Application launcher section

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
#                       Button Event Function Definitions
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Left click   - button 1 
# Middle click - button 2
# Right click  - button 3
# Wheel up     - button 4
# Wheel down   - button 5 
#
# changeDesktop(x)
# - Change Desktop: Increase or decrease the current desktop by 'x' amount
# 
# toggleShade(task)
# - Shade or Unshade an application
#
# toggleHidden()
# - Minimize the panel to the top or bottom depending on its start location
#
# toggleMinimize(task, traise=1)
# - Minimize or Unminimize an application and optionally raise it
#
# taskRaise(task, focus=1)
# - Raise an application to the top of the window list and optionally focus it 
#
# taskLower(task, focus=0)
# - Lower an app to the bottom of the window list and optionally focus it
#
# taskFocus(task)
# - Give focus to the selected application, if it has focus then minimize it
#
# showDesktop()
# - Toggle between hiding and unhiding ALL applications
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#----------------------------------
def desktopButtonEvent(pp, button):
#----------------------------------
    """ Button event handler for the panel's desktop object """
        
    if button == 1:
        pp.changeDesktop(-1)
    elif button == 2:
        pp.changeDesktop(2)
    elif button == 3:
        pp.changeDesktop(1)
    elif button == 4:
        pp.changeDesktop(1)
    elif button == 5:
        pp.changeDesktop(-1)
        
#--------------------------------
def clockButtonEvent(pp, button):
#--------------------------------
    """ Button event handler for the panel's clock object """
    
    if button == 1:
        os.system("xclock &")
    elif button == 2:
        pass
    elif button == 3:
        pp.toggleHidden()  
    elif button == 4:
        pp.showDesktop()
    elif button == 5:
        pp.showDesktop()
        
#--------------------------------
def panelButtonEvent(pp, button):
#--------------------------------
    """ Button event handler for the panel with no active tasks """
    
    if button == 1:
        pass
    elif button == 2:
        pass
    elif button == 3:
        pass
    elif button == 4:
        pass
    elif button == 5:
        pass
        
#-------------------------------------
def taskButtonEvent(pp, button, task):
#-------------------------------------
    """ Button event handler for the panel's tasks """
    
    if button == 1:
        pp.taskFocus(task)
        pp.taskFocus(task)
    elif button == 2:
        # Destroy the application
        task.obj.destroy()
    elif button == 3:
        # Ex. - XMMS doesn't shade, so we want to minimize it instead and
        #       still use button 3 to shade other applications
        #       task.tclass is the tasks class name (WM_CLASS)
        if "xmms" in task.tclass:
            pp.toggleMinimize(task)
        else:
            pp.toggleShade(task)
    elif button == 4:
        pp.taskRaise(task, focus=1)
    elif button == 5:
        pp.taskLower(task, focus=0)
 
```

### Post by RiceMonster on 2008-06-28
Openbox is really simple. You just have to do a bit of reading to learn it.

Try the openbox site:
[http://icculus.org/openbox/index.php/Main_Page](http://icculus.org/openbox/index.php/Main_Page)

and Urukrama's guide:
[http://urukrama.wordpress.com/openbox-guide/](http://urukrama.wordpress.com/openbox-guide/)

---

### Post by ad_267 on 2008-06-29
> **blackvd said:**
> Can't seem to find a matching gtk and emerald i like. Only problem with this one is the window buttons being on the other side.

That's easy to fix. In the Emerald theme manager go to edit themes - titlebar and change the Title-bar Object Layout
